          <img alt="" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.0.0" height="600" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcff1aaec7043ea46bcf_t-summer-movies-head-to-head-emma-stone-george-clooney-melissa-mccarthy-tom-hardy.jpg" width="900"/>
          <figcaption class="caption main-image-caption" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.0.1" style="max-width:900px;">
           <span data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.0.1.0">
           </span>
           <div class="credits" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.0.1.1">
            Courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures (Stone); Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures (Clooney);  2015 Twentieth Century Fox (McCarthy and Hardy).
           </div>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <div class="dek" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.2">
          From Tom Hardy vs. Anna Kendrick to Meryl Streep vs. Miles Teller, its a summer full of strange rivals. How should you choose?
         </div>
         <div class="byline" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3">
          <div class="contributors" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3.$Author">
           <label data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3.$Author.0">
            by
           </label>
           <ul class="list" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3.$Author.1">
            <li class="contributor" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3.$Author.1.$52cc4ed3110a545e44000007">
             <a class="author" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.3.$Author.1.$52cc4ed3110a545e44000007.0" href="/contributor/katey-rich" rel="author">
              Katey Rich
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
         </div>
         <span class="content" data-reactid=".6e5qrlor28.5.1:2.1.0.0.5">
          <p>
           Some summer movies are so gigantic that nothing dares open against them --
           <em>
            The Avengers: Age of Ultron
           </em>
           had the first weekend in May to itself, and
           <em>
            Jurassic World
           </em>
           s dinos will roam alone come June 12. But as summer movie season gets bigger and more crowded every year, the competition gets tougher, and some weekends bring showdowns between some seriously powerful forces. Often these kinds of pairings work great, like when both
           <em>
            Mamma Mia!
           </em>
           and
           <em>
            The Dark Knight
           </em>
           opened huge
           <a href="http://www.boxofficemojo.com/weekend/chart/?yr=2008&amp;wknd=29&amp;p=.htm">
            on the same weekend
           </a>
           in 2008. But sometimes they give moviegoers some tough decisions. So which stars will be forcing you to choose between them this summer, and how many weekends will you just have to go to the theater twice? Behold, our guide to the biggest and best showdowns of summer movie season 2015.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcee1aaec7043ea46ae5_summer-movies-head-to-head-mad-max-pitch-perfect-2-01.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               1.) Left, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures; Right,  2015 Universal Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Tom Hardy vs. Anna Kendrick (May 15)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Mad Max: Fury Road
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Pitch Perfect 2
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A post-apocalyptic wasteland full of weirdos and souped-up cars vs. a hilarious a cappella group
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Resurrecting a popular but dormant action franchise vs. turning an unlikely comedy hit into its own franchise
          </p>
          <p>
           Our first matchup is the first of what will become a familiar summertime battle: boy movie vs. girl movie, with a grim-faced Tom Hardy repping for the boys and Anna Kendrick leading her all-girl a cappella group. (Be prepared for surprises, though; after all, Eve Ensler
           <a href="http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2015/05/mad-max-fury-road-eve-ensler-feminist-triumph">
            was a consultant
           </a>
           on
           <em>
            Mad Max
           </em>
           .  While
           <em>
            Max
           </em>
           , with its eye-popping action, may have the pile everyone in the car and buy lots of popcorn blockbuster edge, the Barden Bellas should not be underestimated.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcfbb80bcc99383a2110_summer-movies-head-to-head-tomorrowland-poltergeist-02.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left,  2015 Twentieth Century Fox; Right, courtesy of Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Sam Rockwell vs. George Clooney (May 22)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Poltergeist
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Tomorrowland
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           The story about a haunted house you might have heard before vs. something secretive about distant worlds and technology and maybe magic?
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           A horror remake that doesnt bring shame upon the first one vs. the increasingly rare summer blockbuster based on an original story
          </p>
          <p>
           In a summer crammed with sure bets and stories that seem obvious based on the trailers, here are two wild cardsa horror remake of a classic but admittedly flawed movie that could maybe use an update, and a large-scale adventure featuring one of Hollywoods biggest stars that has managed to keep much of its plot under wraps. Rockwell (who co-stars with Rosemarie DeWitt) may not be a mega-star like Clooney, but horror movies have had a
           <a href="http://www.boxofficemojo.com/movies/?id=conjuring.htm">
            solid summer track record lately
           </a>
           , which makes this look like a fair fight to us.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fceb1aaec7043ea46ab9_summer-movies-head-to-head-aloha-san-andreas-03.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left,  2015 Columbia Pictures; Right, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Emma Stone vs. The Rock (May 29)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Aloha
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            San Andreas
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A new Cameron Crowe movie vs. The Rock fighting earthquakes
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           A comeback for a filmmaker in need of one vs. a continued victory lap for one of our best modern movie stars
As different as these two movies may seem, theyre essentially the same pitch at their corecome see Cameron Crowe/The Rock do the thing hes great at! Crowes forte happens to be witty rom-coms and The Rocks happens to be witty muscle-flexing, which honestly makes both of these movies sound like great choicesespecially considering that Crowes film stars charisma-packed Stone and Bradley Cooper, some of the only actors alive who can hold the screen as well as The Rock can at his best.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcf61aaec7043ea46b49_summer-movies-head-to-head-spy-entourage-04.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures; Right,  2015 Twentieth Century Fox.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Jeremy Piven vs. Melissa McCarthy (June 5)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Entourage
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Spy
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           Vinny Chase and the boys are back! vs. James Bond, if James Bond were hilarious and also Melissa McCarthy
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Proving the staying power of a show thats been off the air for four years vs.
           <a href="http://variety.com/2015/film/festivals/sxsw-film-review-melissa-mccarthy-in-spy-1201453420/">
            living up to the SXSW hype
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           Heres another boy movie vs. girl movie, though both the
           <em>
            Entourage
           </em>
           series and Melissa McCarthys previous movies were big enough hits that both have obviously broader audiences. Still, we can imagine a lot of date-night couples splitting into separate theaters for these two, re-uniting at the end of the night for the tale of what kind of shenanigans both Ari Gold and Melissa McCarthy got into this time.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fceeb80bcc99383a20b8_summer-movies-head-to-head-magic-mike-terminator-genisys-05.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures; Right, courtesy of Paramount Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Channing Tatum vs. Emilia Clarke (July 1)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Magic Mike XXL
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Terminator: Genisys
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A sequel to an unexpected hit about male strippers vs. a sequel to an unexpected hit about a time-traveling robot that also turned into a franchise about a future war between humans and machines and . . . you know what, its complicated
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Channing Tatum, Movie Star vs.
           <em>
            Terminator
           </em>
           : Movie Franchise
          </p>
          <p>
           Its pretty spectacular that the movie about strippers stars the guy, while the movie about killer robots stars the woman, proving that just when you think youve got summer movie season figured out, they throw some twists in there. The
           <em>
            Terminator
           </em>
           movie gets the box-office edge based on sheer number of explosions, but based on the huge surprise success of the first
           <em>
            Magic Mike
           </em>
           , anything seems possible for the second go-round.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcebb80bcc99383a208c_summer-movies-head-to-head-ant-man-tranwreck-06.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures; Right,  2015 Universal Studios.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Paul Rudd vs. Amy Schumer (July 17)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Ant-Man
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Trainwreck
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A superhero whose power is shrinking down to the size of an ant vs. a rom-com about a woman who is a disaster, but not too disastrous to earn the affection of Bill Hader
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Living up to the legacy of
           <em>
            Guardians of the Galaxy
           </em>
           /
           <em>
            The Avengers
           </em>
           /the entire Marvel Cinematic Universe vs. living up to the incredible hype around both the film and Schumer herself
          </p>
          <p>
           Its almost sad to see Paul Rudd facing off against Amy Schumer, since under any other circumstances wed want to pair the two of them in a
           <em>
            Trainwreck
           </em>
           -style rom-com. (Sequel!?!) As usual, the superhero movie gets the immediate box-office edge in this showdown, but dont underestimate a great summer comedys
           <a href="http://www.boxofficemojo.com/movies/?id=wiigapatow.htm">
            staying power
           </a>
           .
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcf2b80bcc99383a20e4_summer-movies-head-to-head-paper-towns-pixels-07.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left,  2014 Twentieth Century Fox; Right, courtesy of Columbia Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Cara Delevingne vs. Adam Sandler (July 24)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Paper Towns
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Pixels
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A boy falls in love with a mysterious girl only for her to disappear vs. an alien invasion that, somehow, takes the form of 80s video games come to life
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Proving that
           <em>
            The Fault in Our Stars
           </em>
           was no fluke and John Greens books make great movies vs. Adam Sandler, action hero?
          </p>
          <p>
           There are few stranger rivals at the summer box office this year, and the audiences for both are already clearly definedteens in the mood for some quirky romance vs. Adam Sandlers massive fan base. How Cara Delevingne, in her first major film role, will fit into the equation is a big mystery. Either way, sounds like theres room for everybody to win during this weekend.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcf31aaec7043ea46b11_summer-movies-head-to-head-mission-impossible-rogue-nation-vacation-08.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Paramount Pictures; Right, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Tom Cruise vs. Ed Helms (July 31)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Mission: Impossible - Rogue Nation
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Vacation
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           The further death-defying adventures of Ethan Hunt and company vs. a new death-defying adventure for the next generation of road-tripping Griswolds
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Living up to the enormous success of the previous three
           <em>
            Mission: Impossible
           </em>
           films vs. proving that a remake of a comedy classic can be a good thing
          </p>
          <p>
           Bonus points to the only summer showdown pair with rhyming titles. Doesnt make it any easier to choose between them, thoughdo you want to be the first to see Tom Cruise dangling off an airplane, or the remarkable prosthetic Chris Hemsworth
           <a href="http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2015/05/vacation-nsfw-trailer">
            showed off in the trailer
           </a>
           ? How can anyone possibly choose??
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcf61aaec7043ea46b40_summer-movies-head-to-head-ricki-and-the-flash-the-fantastic-four-09.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Twentieth Century Fox Film Corporation; Right,  2015 Sony Pictures Entertainment.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Miles Teller vs. Meryl Streep (August 7)
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            Fantastic Four
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Ricki and the Flash
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           A new origin story for the quartet of superpowered heroes vs. a washed-up wanna-be rock star who tries to reconnect with the family shed left behind
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Yet another new superhero franchise tries to get off the ground despite some worrying buzz vs. can the Meryl Streep
           <a href="http://www.boxofficemojo.com/people/chart/?id=merylstreep.htm">
            summer-hit streak
           </a>
           continue?
          </p>
          <p>
           Another unlikely duo sharing this weekend, and yet another duo wed actually somehow like to see in a rom-com. (What?? That 40-year age gap between Teller and Streep is
           <em>
            nothing
           </em>
           .) The idea is that the superhero-heads go into one theater, the Streep (and Jonathan Demme!) fanatics go into another, and only meet when awkwardly waiting in line together for popcorn.
          </p>
          <div class="embed image landscape row ">
           <figure class="embedded-image">
            <img alt="" border="0" src="http://photos.vanityfair.com/2015/05/11/5550fcfb1aaec7043ea46b95_summer-movies-head-to-head-the-man-from-uncle-straight-outta-compton-10.jpg" title=""/>
            <figcaption classname="caption callout-image-caption">
             <div class="wrapper">
              <div class="credits">
               Left, courtesy of Warner Bros. Pictures; Right,  2015 Universal Studios.
              </div>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
          </div>
          <h2>
           Armie Hammer and Henry Cavill vs. O'Shea Jackson Jr.
          </h2>
          <p>
           <strong>
            The titles:
           </strong>
           <em>
            The Man from U.N.C.L.E.
           </em>
           vs.
           <em>
            Straight Outta Compton
           </em>
           <br/>
           <strong>
            The stories:
           </strong>
           An updated version of the spy series from the 60s vs. a biopic about the seminal rap group NWA
           <strong>
            The stakes:
           </strong>
           Hoping director Guy Ritchie can recapture the energy that went into his
           <em>
            Sherlock Holmes
           </em>
           movies vs. hoping NWAs relatively recent history is ready for the biopic treatment
          </p>
          <p>
           We close out the summer with two more wildcards: a movie based on a series no one remembers all that well and a serious-looking biopic about rap, a genre rarely addressed in serious biopic format. August is so far awaywho even knows which of these will prevail at this point?
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            WATCH: Go Behind the Scenes of Our 2015 Hollywood Portfolio
           </strong>
          </p>

            </iframe>
           </div>
          </div>
